Investigation of the Korean Incident (Continued) 73

The True Face of the Japanese Side: Japan's plan for Korea is to adopt a policy of gradual immigration, moving Korean people to the Northeast to live with Chinese people, making the Northeast a semi-colonial area. They want to free up a piece of land in Korea and move the surplus Japanese population there. Unexpectedly, Chinese people have not known how to advance or retreat in recent years and have continued to immigrate, filling the positions vacated by the Korean people. Before the Japanese people can move in, the Chinese people have already taken their place, sharing some profits each year and sending them back to China. This is especially disliked by the masters. Therefore, Japanese newspapers, such as the Keijo Nippo, the organ of the Government-General of Korea, repeatedly publish news about the number of Chinese people entering Korea and affecting the livelihood of Korean people. At the same time, the Korean newspapers, such as the Korean Ilbo and the Chosun Ilbo, promote the idea that hundreds of thousands of Chinese people reside in Korea, sharing 40 to 50 million in profits each year and sending them back to China. This is all the blood and sweat of the Korean people, which is being scraped away by the Chinese people. They should quickly find ways to prevent this. Therefore, Korean people have gradually become hostile to Chinese people. The Government-General of Korea has used labor permits to restrict the entry of Chinese people. When Chinese people enter Korea, they are neither prevented nor rejected. Those who want to work or set up businesses must obtain a certificate. Each certificate is only valid for one year. Whether they will be allowed to obtain another certificate after the expiration date is up to the government to consider. Therefore, the lives of Chinese people are even more difficult. Each time a certificate is presented, it is delayed and not issued until the Chinese people cannot survive and are forced to return to their country. The Seoul-Incheon Chamber of Commerce has repeatedly appealed for this passive anti-Chinese method and requested the Japanese side to clearly order the prohibition of Chinese people from entering Korea to avoid the侨胞 futile travel back and forth. The Japanese government seems to be concerned about the great powers and is unwilling to issue such an order. In the early spring of this year, many Chinese people had already arrived in Seoul and Incheon. Due to the restrictions of the Japanese authorities, they were trapped for many days and had no choice but to return to their country. Those who did not come saw the Japanese side's rejection and stopped. On the Japanese side, they are also unwilling to use public words to offend the world. After hesitating repeatedly, they used the Wanpaoshan incident to fabricate rumors of Korean people being harmed and to make the ignorant and uninformed Korean people engage in indirect anti-Chinese behavior. When the Wanpaoshan incident occurred, the Japanese side immediately designated the Keijo Nippo as a monthly chronicle of evil propaganda, publishing news every day about Chinese people oppressing Korean farmers and expelling Korean people from the Northeast provinces. The Korean people, unaware, gnashed their teeth and clenched their fists at the Chinese people, deliberately looking for trouble. Half a month ago, there were several incidents of conflict between Chinese and Korean people every day. On July 1st, Changchun farmers dug up the ditch. The Japanese side believed that the opportunity had arrived and reported to the Japanese Consulate in Changchun that Chinese farmers and police had surrounded Korean farmers and beaten several people to death. The Chosun Ilbo published an extra edition based on this information. Although the newspaper published a report by Special Commissioner Kim Tatsuo, saying that Kim was killed by Changchun farmers, in fact, Kim never reported it and was innocently killed. The anger of the Korean people, which had been accumulating for a long time, was vented in one day. However, at first, they did not dare to beat people, only throwing stones and smashing windows. Later, seeing that the Japanese police not only did not stop them, but also helped them, they became bolder and started to beat people. The original intention of the Japanese side was to make the Korean people riot and beat the Chinese people, creating panic and making the Chinese people flee in fear. They did not know that what was released by me would not listen to my orders when recovered. The Korean people became excited about beating and killing, and it became their pleasure to kill and set fire. The tragedy in Pyongyang was caused by this reason. Although Japan deliberately showed calmness afterward, it was because the Korean people's riot had gradually exceeded its expected range. It was also afraid that they would unite and act against Japan, so it tried its best to suppress them. Later, the Japanese police in various places armed themselves and came out to protect them in earnest. It should be known that this was not a sincere protection of the Chinese people, but entirely for their own sake. Although their plan has fortunately succeeded, they feel guilty in their hearts and are afraid that it will be difficult to explain to China and to the great powers. Therefore, they are trying their best to comfort the wounded and dead and to cover up their actions. However, everyone knows Sima Zhao's intentions.

The True Heart of the Korean People: The Korean people have no independent opinions. Those over middle age express goodwill towards Chinese people. Based on historical relations, they call Chinese people "Taeilguk Saram" (i.e., people of a great country) and have always been friendly. Those under middle age have been influenced by Japanese education and look down on Chinese people, calling Chinese people "Chungguk Saram" or "Jina Saram," which is still respectful. Otherwise, they directly call them "long necks" (meaning "Please Please Thing" in Japanese, which comes from the Chinese people saying "Please Please" when being polite). Children especially like to intercept Chinese people on the street and call them that to their faces. Chinese people are greedy for the easy profits in the area, so even if they are humiliated, they cannot bear to leave. Sometimes Korean people gather in restaurants, order wine and food, and after eating and drinking their fill, they push and refuse to pay the owner. Even if they are arrested and detained by the Japanese police station, the Chinese merchants have already suffered losses. However, this is only a common occurrence and has no major relationship with this tragedy. The greatest cause of this incident is the increasing number of Chinese people entering Korea. The labor is cheap and hardworking. The daily wage of Korean workers is one yuan, while the daily wage of Chinese workers is only five jiao. In terms of work, such as loading and unloading cars at the dock, six Chinese workers can load and unload one car per day. If Korean workers are used instead, even eight people cannot complete the job in one day. Therefore, Chinese workers are welcomed by employers. Even Korean business owners hire Chinese workers. In addition, Korean people are lazy by nature. They often take breaks from work. After working for a few days and earning a small amount of money, they give up and play for a few days, waiting until they have spent all their money before continuing to work. Such laziness is naturally not welcomed. Therefore, the number of Chinese workers in Korea is increasing day by day. Stevedores can earn two yuan per day. Those with expertise, such as carpenters and tilers, can earn twice as much. Korean people see us as cheap, but we Chinese see the profit as several times higher than in our country. Korean people are clumsy and have simple skills. There are very few carpenters and tilers. The work they do is slow and clumsy, far inferior to our workers. Therefore, our carpenters and tilers also have considerable influence in Korea. The status of Chinese workers is increasing day by day, and they are gradually being valued. At the same time, the number of Korean people who are being displaced and unemployed is also increasing day by day. They are jealous and resentful of Chinese people and are thinking of taking the opportunity to vent their anger. The Japanese are also stirring up trouble and inciting them, causing the Korean people under middle age to want to strike a blow and enjoy themselves. Most of those who participated in the atrocities on the day of the incident were workers and students. Korean people over the age of forty did not approve of this. When they encountered Chinese people fleeing, they would hide them or change their clothes and send them out of the border. Therefore, many Chinese people were able to escape thanks to them. After the great massacre in Pyongyang, various groups organized by the general public expressed great sympathy for the Chinese people, sending money and food to comfort the wounded and dead dozens or hundreds of times. When they met Chinese people, they would apologize. The peace in various places is not due to the maintenance of the Japanese side, but entirely due to the buffer effect of these groups.

Qingdao All Circles Anti-Japanese and Aid Overseas Chinese General Assembly 74

Overseas Chinese Returning Home Give a Speech on the Beginning and End of the Disaster

The General Assembly Passed Seven Important Proposals

Qingdao Correspondence: The city's various circles opened an anti-Japanese and aid overseas Chinese general assembly at the Qi Yan Hall at 10:00 AM this morning (30th). About 3,000 people attended. The venue was filled with various slogans. Wu Zunming, the chairman of the city's guidance committee, first reported on the significance of the meeting. Next, Wu Yonggong, a Chinese overseas Chinese who had returned home after suffering, reported on the beginning and end of the Korean people's riot and witnessed the tragic situation. His speech was tragic and impassioned, and those who heard it were furious. Then, Huang Shaoxian, the representative of the academic circles, and Zhang Yutian, the representative of the Chamber of Commerce, gave speeches. Finally, seven proposals were passed, and the meeting ended with a high call of slogans. The passed cases are recorded as follows: (1) Telegraph to the National Government to negotiate seriously with Japan to resist to the end, and the citizens of this city are willing to be the backing. (2) Telegraph to the whole country to unanimously conduct economic severance with Japan. (3) Telegraph to comfort the overseas Chinese in Korea. (4) The Qingdao Anti-Japanese and Aid Overseas Chinese Committee will be organized by various groups and schools in Qingdao, and the Qingdao Municipal Party Department, the Jiaoji Railway Special Party Department, Qingdao University, Qingdao Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Journalists Association, Lawyers Association, Women's Zhengyi Association, and the National Goods Movement Committee will be elected as standing committee members to be responsible for planning and implementing the anti-Japanese and aid overseas Chinese work. (5) Please telegraph to the whole country to unanimously refuse to use Japanese currency and implement economic salvation of the country. (6) Please ask the comrades of the business community in this city to withdraw from the Stock Exchange and organize their own exchanges in order to seek the fundamental development of Chinese commerce. (7) Please ask all circles to organize domestic goods factories and ask the government to exempt or reduce domestic goods tax in order to thoroughly boycott Japanese goods. (July 30th)

Ever-Increasing Water Levels in the Canal 75

The two factions of upholding and opening the Cheluo Dam are in fierce dispute.

The Commissioner of Civil Affairs of Jiangsu Province heads to Gaobao to inspect.

A dispatch from Yangzhou reports that the water level in the canal has been rising dramatically in recent days. From July 30th to August 1st, the Shao Bo area under the jurisdiction of Gaobao and Jiangdu counties has seen a continuous rise in water levels.

Page 10

Residents along the canal are in a state of panic and confusion. Yesterday morning (July 31st), our reporter chartered a boat from Yangzhou northward (because steamships and automobiles had long since stopped running). As the boat passed Wantou, ten li from Yangzhou, the waterline was gradually approaching the shore. Upon reaching Shao Bo, the distance between the shore and the water was only about one foot. Many sandbags had been placed on the east bank. Entering the Gaoyou County boundary, the distance between the water and the shore became even closer. Arriving at Cheluo in You at 5 PM, there were many people on the shore. We disembarked and asked about the water level. According to them, on the 29th, it was one zhang, seven chi, and four cun. On the 30th, it rose sharply by four cun. Today (the 31st), it has risen another five fen. Judging by the situation, it is feared that it will continue to rise. We further investigated the number of people on the shore. Between Cheluo and Gaoyou County, a distance of twenty li, there were about three or four thousand people. Besides one-third being from Gaoyou, the rest had dialects from the lower river counties, such as Xinghua, Dongtai, and Yancheng. Further inquiries revealed that the county magistrates, members of the county party headquarters, heads of various bureaus, and representatives of various public organizations from the above counties were all gathered there, taking turns supervising the laborers to protect the dike and strictly guarding the Cheluo Dam, fearing that the people of Gaoyou would secretly open it and cause the lower river to be flooded. Many reed mat sheds were built along the bank, and open-air stalls selling sesame cakes and steamed buns filled the dike. The two factions of upholding and opening the dam were like warring states, facing each other in a tense standoff. Wang Long, the magistrate of Gaoyou County, Li Zhongqiang, the director of the engineering office, and officials and gentry from the lower river counties were consulting back and forth, planning to open half of the Cheluo Dam, seeking only to keep the water level along the canal even with the shore. However, the people of Xinghua and other counties swore they would never allow it. The magistrate of Xinghua County was particularly vehement in the dispute. Wu Tongju, the director of the canal engineering office, was also in Gaoyou. Mao Yisheng, the director of the water conservancy bureau, went to Bao on the 30th, as the two hundred or so li along the canal from Baoying to Shaobo Town in Jiangdu were the most dangerous. They were divided into sections: Baoying, Sishui, Yong'an, Gaoyou, and Jiangdu. Each section, known as one of the five downstream sections, had a section chief and several staff members. Every li had a defense work shed manned by five people, known as shed guards. A golden yellow flag was erected on each shed, with black characters saying "Defense Work Section No. X Shed". The reason why the flag was golden yellow was because golden yellow is similar to earth color, implying that earth can overcome water. Near each shed, there were piles of earth and reeds of varying heights. If the dike were to crack, they would be used for emergency repairs. If the crack was large, while making emergency repairs, the shed guards would rush to report to other sheds to the north and south, so that they could concentrate on the cracked area and work together to protect it. The preparations were said to be very thorough. Regarding the issue of upholding or opening the dam, Commissioner Hu of the Department of Civil Affairs was expected to arrive from Zhenjiang the day after tomorrow (August 2nd) to first inspect the Jiang'an bank in Guazhou, and then go to You to investigate the situation, so as to weigh the pros and cons and make a decision on whether to open or uphold the dam. Our reporter originally intended to go to Baoying again, but because the water level upstream was even higher and the boat could not move forward, we returned to Yangzhou this morning (August 1st). After arriving in Yangzhou, we received a long-distance call from Gaoyou that the water level at Yuma Wharf had reached one zhang and eight chi. The Jiangsu Pacification Superintendent's Office telegraphed the provincial government's Director Li Mingyangshi: "Opening the dam would cause significant losses. The province has decided to focus on protecting the assigned personnel, namely, Wu Tongju, Director of the Canal Engineering Office, and Mao Yisheng, Director of the Water Conservancy Bureau. Please immediately instruct your subordinate troops to cooperate and maintain it. Deeply grateful." After Superintendent Zhang approved the telegram, he immediately telegraphed Chief Commander Liang in Qingjiang and the brigade commander stationed in Yangzhou to comply and provide assistance. In addition, along the road from Yangzhou to Taixian, the three bridges of Dong, Shi, and Liao, which we passed, were extremely long, requiring more than 300,000 yuan for construction. In the past two days, the Dong and Shi bridges had been completely washed away by the flood. The longest Liao Bridge (i.e., Wanfu Bridge) is now tilting southward and is impassable. It is expected to collapse within half a day. The long-distance bus routes between Yangzhou and Zhenjiang, and Yangzhou and Zhongjiang have been damaged by the rain and have been impassable for a week. The long-distance telephone line across the river between Yangzhou and Zhenjiang has also been cut off by the river tide. If the dikes along the canal unfortunately collapse again, the lives and property of dozens of counties will suffer even greater losses. (August 1st)

Heartbreaking and Tragic Flooding in Jiangpu 76

A dispatch from Nanjing reports that Jiangpu, facing the Yangtze River and bordering Anhui Province, has been plagued by continuous rain for the past month, causing mountain torrents to erupt. Most of the polder fields in the northern part of the area have been breached, and countless people have been swept away. What's worse, on the 23rd and 24th of last month, heavy rain poured down, day and night, and the Jiaohong River from the eight hundred li Huangshan Mountains in northern Anhui overflowed and flowed straight down. All the polder dikes and embankments were washed away. Even flatland towns such as Chahe, Dongge, Yongning, and Tangquan were several zhang deep in water. As a result, more than ten li of the Jinpu Railway foundation was washed away, and the train was stopped for about four or five days. The area was a vast expanse of water, with no boundaries. People, livestock, and belongings were all swept away. Cries shook the ground, and the scene was too tragic to bear. The flood victims climbing the treetops were rescued by emergency relief, while no fewer than several thousand people, supporting the old and carrying the young, moved to the mountains to take refuge, eating in the wind and sleeping in the open, and crying for food. Those who were unable to escape the raging flood and drowned were also everywhere. The scale of this catastrophe is unprecedented. Currently, local gentry Ye Chuliang (Director of the World Red Swastika Society) and local enthusiasts Gu Jinbo, Lin Chunting, Wu Heting, Lou Xiaokuan, Xu Rangsan, Gu Laixi, etc., concerned about the severity of the disaster, specially invited the county relief branch, the Chamber of Commerce, the relief hospital, the Red Cross, and other organizations to organize the Jiangpu Flood Emergency Relief Association. They temporarily raised more than a thousand yuan in silver and two hundred bags of flour (issued by the Xiaguan Red Swastika Society) to carry out emergency relief. They also led a steamboat and went to the disaster area to provide relief. They have been working day and night, extremely busy. No fewer than several hundred people in the border area of Liuhe (Yueliang, Shuangcheng, and other polders), who were connected to Pu and received the same relief, were able to save their lives. In addition to actively carrying out relief work, the association has also sent Xu Rangsan, Gu Laixi, etc., to various government offices and charitable organizations in the province and Shanghai to appeal, report on the disaster, and request emergency assistance.

Wuhu Quick Dispatch 77

The various circles' flood relief association held a meeting at the county government yesterday. To expand the fundraising efforts, all leaders of various organizations and chairmen of various trade associations were made members. Zhao, the chief of public security bureau, Magistrate Yu, and Lu, the manager of the Shanghai Bank, and other fifteen people were mutually elected as executive members. The provincial government has already sent a telegram, first allocating 1,000 yuan, instructing proper implementation of urgent relief, and notifying various entertainment venues to jointly organize a flood relief entertainment meeting after the flood recedes. Currently, in addition to the association, various charitable organizations and private individuals have already started to collect donations, distribute rice tickets and money tickets, and provide pot crust porridge, etc. The price of rice has risen sharply by several yuan in the past two days, with inferior rice already selling for 13 yuan per dan. The party headquarters has requested the public security bureau to quickly stop it to reassure the people.

In recent days, no fewer than ten thousand disaster-stricken people from neighboring counties and villages have come to Wuhu to flee the famine, and they are everywhere. For the sake of local security, the military and police authorities have implemented a curfew every night from 11:00 PM, setting up posts to check pedestrians, and dispatching water patrols to patrol the streets. Last night, the power company, the telephone bureau, and the telegraph bureau all sent troops to guard the area, which was extremely tight. The provincial government has also ordered the provincial shipping office to send armed patrol boats to Wuhu to patrol the river and maintain local security.

Yuxi, a place in Hexian County, twenty li from Wuhu, is a necessary area for rice boats from the province to come and go, and commerce is very prosperous. However, the night before, fifty or sixty bandits suddenly arrived, carrying weapons, and rushed to the town, intending to rob the self-defense group of their guns. The enclosure, knowing it was outnumbered, had already taken their weapons and fled in advance. The bandits then went from house to house robbing, and only left fully loaded after several hours. More than a hundred stores, such as Ruhe Shengxiang and Tonghechun, were robbed, with losses of about tens of thousands of taels of silver.

Wanzhi and Xih River, two major towns in Wuhu, were already heavily flooded, but the night before, Jiaolong river suddenly occurred, and the water rose more than a zhang high, rushing straight in. More than fifty stores in Xi River were destroyed, and more than a hundred people died.

At Lubin Port and Pangxie Creek in Wuhu, it was previously discovered that bandits had colluded with hundreds of refugees to rob passing rice boats and travelers, and planned to encircle and rob the Lubin Port Defense Corps of their guns. The group commander came to Wuhu for help, and the 171st Brigade of the 57th Division immediately sent a company of soldiers on a special ship. They scattered the bandits, captured eight bandits, and seized a wheat boat that had been robbed. They have already been sent to Wuhu for interrogation. (August 2nd)

Local Correspondence

Fengxian 78

Woman willingly commits adultery with her father, who accuses her of abduction. Lu Hanwen, a farmer from the 33rd map of Dongxiang in the county, had an affair with Yun Gu, the eldest daughter of Chen Musen from the same map. He divorced his wife and eloped with the woman on March 28th of the 18th year to live in Shanghai. Although Chen sued the county at that time, he was never found because his address was unknown. Now, Hanwen thought that things had passed and the affair had cooled down and would be understood. He returned with the woman to his hometown on the 23rd of last month to recognize his maternal uncle. Unexpectedly, Musen was ashamed and indignant when he saw this situation, and immediately twisted the man and woman together to the county government, requesting the law to investigate the matter. The Eastern Office's judge, Tong, opened the court for trial. According to the confession, both Yun Gu and the other said that they had cohabited voluntarily, and the Chen family had come to the face-to-face to admit it. At the same time, Yun Gu also confessed that she was willing to run away with Hanwen. Her father had been to her home in Shanghai for meals and money. This time, however, it was because she had listened to others, intending to sell her elsewhere, etc. However, Judge Tong believes that although the matter is voluntary, the previous and subsequent procedures have not been legally handled. Therefore, in addition to putting Yun Gu on bail, he ordered her to continue to verify and take the matter into his hands.

The county's drug rehabilitation center is officially opened. The county's drug rehabilitation center has been entrusted by County Magistrate Shen to the county's clinic, which was established on August 1. Its nature is specifically for forced rehabilitation. Therefore, all smokers are completely forcibly sent by the county government. The number is temporarily limited to 30 people due to the number of beds. Of these, 15 people will be charged for food and lodging, at five yuan per person. The remaining smoking case fines will be used to subsidize the drug rehabilitation center. In terms of organization, County Magistrate Shen Qingchen is the supervisor, while the clinic director Diao Yebai and Western medicine director Hu Dacai are responsible for the administration and medical affairs on a voluntary basis.

For a time, ignorant men and women from far and near flocked to seek oracles. More than a dozen boats a day are hired from farther away. Suzhou 81

The bandit suppression department searched the incense shop. Because of a secret report, the Taihu bandit suppression headquarters sent a platoon of soldiers from the 9th Company to surround the Shengxiangyun Incense Shop at No. 72, Dajie Street, outside Xumen, at about 2:00 AM yesterday morning (August 3rd), as there were hidden guns and other items. They implemented a search, but found nothing. Pan Jinrong (78 years old) and his son, Pan Guibao (35 years old), were tied up and sent to the headquarters for strict interrogation. The shops there said that the incense shop has been open for decades and that the owner has always been law-abiding. This search also found nothing. They plan to jointly submit a request to the command headquarters for bail to avoid harming innocent people.

The appeal in the Refining Company's murder-for-money case opened. Xu Kuijun, an accountant at the Shanghai Refining Company, was murdered by trainee Shi Ruiqing on January 3 of this year. He secretly opened the iron box and stole more than 1,300 yuan. At the time, it was suspected that Zhou Awu, who worked in the shop, was the perpetrator. Zhou Awu was sent to the Shanghai District Court. Later, because Shi Ruiqing suddenly fled, it was learned that Shi was the murderer. Shi was found and handed over to the court. After the Shanghai Court's judgment, Zhou Awu and Shi Ruiqing were accomplices and were both sentenced to death. Shi and Zhou refused to accept the verdict and appealed to the High Court. Yesterday (August 3rd), Chen Dexin, the manager of the nuclear company, and others were summoned to court. The summons were issued after passing through the hunger period, and people were summoned to open the court again.

The new county magistrate took office today. Huang Suishen, the magistrate of Wu County, resigned with approval. His successor is Wu Jia, the current magistrate of Wujiang County. The new County Magistrate Wu arrived in Su yesterday (August 3rd). At 11:00 AM, he went to the county government to visit County Magistrate Huang to discuss handover procedures. It was decided that he would officially take office today at the morning of God's affairs.

The Dumb Lover's new film prosecution case was appealed. Because the Xi Fan Film Company produced the sensational "Dumb Lover" film, the family members of Lin Jiemu and others sued the Shanghai Court, and the manager, Ren Xifan, was convicted of defamation and fined 400 yuan, and the director, Chen Zhuomin, was fined 200 yuan. Ren and Chen refused to accept the verdict and filed a petition with the Suzhou High Prosecutor's Office. Yesterday (August 3rd), it was approved that the appeal should be filed with the original trial court. The appeal was ordered to be sent to the Shanghai District Court for verification and handling.

Wuxi 82

A tofu merchant's funeral was stolen of a large sum of money. According to local customs, when an elderly person dies, relatives and friends do not wear mourning clothes on the day of the funeral. Also, when returning to the house (i.e., returning home), they must enter through a red and green door. They should wear silk clothes and red skirts, and wear gold, silver, and jewelry on their heads to show the breadth of the scene. Zhu Ronggeng, the owner of a tofu shop at No. 14 Qingguoxiang, had saved some money in his life. He died of illness in late last month, and yesterday was the day of his funeral. Several relatives and friends packed red skirts, silk clothes, beads, gold, silver, jewelry, etc., in a large leather bag, intending to bring them to the cemetery for use when returning home. Unexpectedly, when the coffin was being carried out, it was stolen by a thief taking advantage of the chaos. In addition to the gold jewelry and clothes, there was also a pearl flower. The total loss was estimated at about 300 yuan.

Mulberry fields are flooded, causing autumn silkworms to die. Since the beginning of summer, the county has been experiencing continuous rain and rising river water. The dikes in the four villages have collapsed one after another, creating an irredeemable ocean. As a result, many mulberry fields have been flooded. Therefore, the autumn silkworm crop will inevitably be greatly reduced. It is reported that the various seed production fields have produced a total of 1.4 million sheets of autumn silkworm eggs. Currently, only 400,000 sheets have been sold. Qingcheng City, Qianzhou, Yuqi, Beiqifang, and other places have all ordered the Tiger Brand seeds from the Dayou Seed Production Field, totaling 360,000 sheets. However, the breeders are currently aware that the mulberry trees are soaked in water, and the mulberry leaves are withered and yellow. Feeding the silkworms with them would be unsuitable. Therefore, they have no intention of raising them and have been returning them to the seed production field.

Jiangyin 83

Villages along the canal are required to pay for dike repair fees. The small passenger boats traveling back and forth along the canal near Qingyang and Yueqiao in the 11th district are collapsing and damaging the banks of the canal, flooding the farmland. Xu Zukun and other representatives of the 11th district have submitted a request to the county to pay 120 yuan per month in dike repair fees from the Zhaoshang Licheng Factory Dongsanzhou Small Boat Company to provide relief. In the afternoon of the 30th, the county government convened a meeting of the manager of the Dongsanzhou Small Boat Company and Wu Fengnian and other representatives of the villages along the canal. After discussion, it was decided that 2,400 yuan would be paid first, from the 18th year to this year, as dike repair fees.

The defendants in the Zhou case separately paid money to close the case. The Zhou Shuiping case has been pending for a long time. The judicial department, the District Court, ruled that the false accusation charge was not established. The case of Zhou Shuiping's compensation was previously resolved by the provincial government meeting that the 38 defendants would pay 2,000 yuan separately. Zhang Lin, Sha Zhixian, Zhang Chongzhi, Zhu Zhenyang, Shi Tai, and Wu Baolian have already paid the money. The money, 10,000 yuan, will be temporarily stored in the county government.

Vagrants in the reformatory rioted. A large number of vagrants escaped from the Wuyi Vagrant Reformatory on the 30th of last month. Yun Mutao and other thirteen people have been captured. However, at noon on the 2nd, the vagrants in the west ward of the institute gathered to riot again. The institute police were unable to stop them and urgently reported to the Public Security Bureau. The director of the bureau, Li Zonggang, personally led the police to the scene to suppress the riot and reprimanded the vagrants. It was later found that Yang Heshang, Tan Fada, Zhang Zidao, and other three people were the leaders of the incident. They were taken to the bureau for interrogation, and the rioting was quelled.

Two corpses, a man and a woman, were found in the fields. The bodies of a man and a woman, stabbed to death, were found in the private road ditch in Gaotou Village, Tangzhou Township, Wuyi County. The chief prosecutor of the county court, Yang, went to the village on the morning of the 2nd to inspect the bodies. It was learned that the female corpse was the wife of Xu San, Zhu, who had been having an affair with Wang Xuhou (the male corpse). Recently, the two people's relationship broke down. Zhu saw that Wang had always tried to avoid him. The other day, Wang hid a sharp blade and saw Zhu working in the field, and rushed forward and stabbed her to death. Then he committed suicide with the knife. After inspecting the corpses, the inspecting official believed that the situation was the same. The official ordered the murder weapon to be taken into the case. The male corpse was collected by his brother, and the female corpse was collected by her husband.

The province orders dike protection, dike reinforcement, and emergency rescue. The canal water level is still rising. A female corpse was found in the official well at the root of the city. Gaoyou 86

Opening the Cheluo Dam was unsuccessful. Because of the rising river water, various legal groups in the county feared that there would be a danger of dike breaks, so they sent a telegram to the provincial government to open the dam. The provincial government approved the opening of half of the dam first. After receiving the telegram, the county authorities sent police officers from the Public Security Bureau and stationed troops in the mail to open the Cheluo Dam. At that time, there were about 5,000 farmers from Xinghua, Taixing, Yancheng, Dong, and the lower river counties who were sleeping on the dam to protect it. Seeing that they wanted to open the dam, the sound of crying shook the sky for a while, and the scene was too tragic to bear. After Xinghua County Magistrate Hua Zhen and Taixing County Magistrate Zhang Yi requested to postpone the opening, and the two county magistrates Hua Zhang gave a painful speech to the public. All the soldiers and police had no choice but to return to the city to report.

Rice prices soar. Because of the increasing water level in the canal, the rice mills in the county feared that the dam would be opened, so they raised the price of rice. In five days, the price of high-quality rice has risen from 10 yuan and 8 jiao to 14 yuan, the price of medium-quality rice has risen from 10 yuan to 13 yuan and 2 jiao, and the price of low-quality rice has risen from 9 yuan and 8 jiao to 12 yuan and 6 jiao. In order to maintain the people's food supply, the county party department yesterday specially sent a letter to the county government to investigate the county's rice and strictly prohibit it from leaving the county, and to prohibit rice merchants from raising prices.

Jiaxing 87

Supervisors illegally arrested. Wang Zongwen and Wen Hongxiang, supervisors of the Jiaxing County Public Security Bureau, led the police to the South Lake the other day. Shi Guixiang, Yang Jinsheng, and Qiu Jingshui jumped from the silk net boat to the ferry boat and were ordered to cross to Yanyu Tower. They were immediately accused of improper behavior, preventing the cable from being unanchored, and coercing Guixiang and the other three, including the boat woman Jinbao, to follow them ashore. Arrested to the bureau, now Guixiang and others are closely related to Wang and Wen, who are close to illegal arrest, and violate the law and misunderstand the criminal law. Moreover, the members and other officials deal with illegal cases and act legally. The Yuan contacted and urgently asked the county government to elect members of the board, or the police officers were committed to court for punishment for breaking the law.

A telegram was sent to announce the expenditures of the district office. The expenses of the Jiaxing District Office were supplemented in the 19th year with a total of 5 jiao per shi and per tael from the grain tax. At that time, county residents Jiang Shitan and Sheng Yuan once telegraphed to exempt the tax. The Finance Department approved the tax for one year in the 19th year. When the tax period expired, it was busy collecting the tax in the 20th year. The county has compiled a summary of the number of surcharges collected, reconciled the revenue and expenditure, and inquired whether to continue to collect the tax, open meetings, and then submit it for approval. The department ordered the county to comply with the case. The county government convened a meeting of a small number of legal representatives a month ago to submit a request to continue to collect the tax because Sheng Yuan and other ten people sent separate telegrams, instructing the county to stop the surcharge, and at the same time, publicly announce the number of collections collected in the 19th year. After the Finance Department received the telegram, it ordered the county government and the Finance Bureau to investigate the original case, review it, and report it for decision.

Yu Xian cracked a kidnapping case. Kidnapping cases have been reported in Yu Xian district in recent months, so the water and land police have paid close attention to the visiting overseas Chinese in the area. Wu Deshun, a water police detective, has now arrested He Haichen and other four suspects in the kidnapping case. The criminals were placed in the district for interrogation, and other crimes were reported.

Huzhou 88

The Qingxiang Bureau Executes Two Bandit Criminals: Two bandits, Lin Laosan and Yu Defu, who previously robbed seven businesses including Lin Yuanfeng Rice Shop in the Wuxing County area and kidnapped three people for ransom, were apprehended by the Zhejiang Water Police 2nd District police and rescued the three hostages, including Fan. Because the crimes occurred in Wuxing, the district police escorted them to the Wuxing Qingxiang Bureau for interrogation. The bureau chief, Li, interrogated them, and the bandits confessed directly. The bureau chief then submitted a request to the Provincial Qingxiang Bureau for the death penalty, and yesterday afternoon at 4 p.m., police were dispatched to the court to retrieve the two criminals, Lin and Yu, verified their identities, tied them up, and executed them by firing squad next to the automobile road at the South Gate.

Villagers Report Continuous Flooding: Li Guangyu, the magistrate of Wuxing County in this city, has been inspecting the countryside for several days due to reports of flooding from farmers in the surrounding areas. Because the affected area is vast, Magistrate Li went to the southern countryside to survey the damage this morning (the 1st), and separately dispatched the Director of Finance and the Director of Public Safety to the northern countryside for inspection. The Director of Finance, Zhou, had just arrived at Baique Village when he was surrounded by the local villagers, who smashed his sedan chair. Also, at around 10 a.m. on the same morning, more than 300 farmers from the 24th and 25th villages at the border of Qingdongmen and Fengshengmen gathered, each carrying farm tools, and swarmed to the Wuxing County Auditorium. The county magistrate was out inspecting the disaster outside the South Gate and had not yet returned. The county section chief came out to meet with Shao Hetai, the village head of the two villages, and advised the farmers to return to their villages and attend to their farms. However, the ignorant villagers remained in the auditorium, raising their farm tools and clamoring incessantly. Before these villagers had dispersed, hundreds of farmers from Jifang Village outside the North Gate, each carrying hoes and shovels, marched in, ringing gongs. The outcome remains unknown.

Hangzhou 89

The Director of the Highway Bureau Assumes Office on Schedule: Huang Airu, Director of the Zhejiang Provincial Highway Administration Bureau, assumed office in March, but suddenly submitted his resignation to the Construction Department due to poor health. It has been approved, and Huang will be transferred to the Construction Department as a technician. Liu Guangxing, the head of the First Section of the department, has been appointed to fill the vacancy. The handover was originally scheduled for yesterday (the 3rd), but due to the various handover procedures not being completed in time, it was rescheduled for the morning of the 5th.

A Large Batch of Red Pills Seized at Nanxing Station: Yesterday (the 3rd) at around 8 a.m., when the No. 1578 screened train from the Shanghai-Hangzhou Zhakou Station arrived at Nanxing Station, members of the Anti-Japanese Association at Zhuqiaotou inspected Japanese goods and discovered a large package of red pills, totaling approximately 50,000 to 60,000 pills. They were sent from Shanghai's Li Jinji to Hong Peiwen's transit business at Haiyue Bridge. Officer Gao, from the Fourth District, happened to be passing by and immediately confiscated them and took them to the police station. He also ordered the owner of the business to be summoned for questioning and telegraphed Shanghai to investigate the sender, so that they could be sent to the court together for legal proceedings.

The Anti-Japanese and Overseas Chinese Aid Association's Methods for Handling Japanese Goods: The Hangzhou Anti-Japanese and Overseas Chinese Aid Association yesterday passed a resolution at its regular meeting stipulating five methods for handling Japanese goods. It specifically notified all businesses, firms, and factories to register with the association. The methods are as follows: (1) Japanese goods paid for and ordered before July 17th will be handled with separate methods. (2) Japanese goods paid for and ordered between July 18th and July 26th (inclusive) will be allowed to be registered and returned, but a registration fee of one-tenth of the original value of the goods will be charged. (3) Japanese goods paid for and ordered between July 27th and July 31st (inclusive) will be allowed to be registered and returned, but a registration fee of two-tenths of the original value of the goods will be charged. (4) All Japanese goods paid for and ordered after August 1st will be confiscated. (5) The registration period will be from August 5th to August 12th. If found after the deadline, they will be confiscated and forfeited.

Shangyu 90

Troops Stationed in Wufu Capture Bandit Gang: Soldiers from the 4th Division of the National Army stationed in Wufu were patrolling the station on the afternoon of the 1st when they noticed eight men resembling farmers, each carrying a bag on their shoulders, acting suspiciously. They stepped forward to question them, but they spoke evasively. The bags were opened, and multiple handguns were discovered. They were immediately surrounded and arrested and sent to headquarters for interrogation and detention.

This City

The Municipal Government Suspends Appropriations 93

Reasons for the County Education Subsidy 94

If Respect is Given to the Resolutions of the Provincial and Municipal Division of Governance Rights Conference

The Various Handover Subsidy Fees Can Still be Appropriated as Usual

Regarding the Shanghai County Party Department's discussion of the Shanghai Municipal Government violating the agreement and owing Shanghai County education fees, a reporter from the East China News Agency went to the Municipal Government to inquire about everything. According to an important official, the Municipal Government previously stopped allocating subsidies to Shanghai and Baoshan counties due to disputes over the division of funds between the province and the city. Later, the Jiangsu Provincial Government repeatedly submitted requests from Shanghai and Baoshan counties to resolve the issue quickly, so it sent personnel to jointly liquidate with the Municipal Government. In addition, with the relocation of the Shanghai County government urgently underway, there was a great need for funds, and a request was made to the Municipal Government to first allocate funds starting from April of this year to maintain essential needs. In addition to sending personnel to jointly liquidate, the Municipal Government replied that it would approve the request and issue subsidies to Shanghai and Baoshan counties uniformly starting from May of this year. As for the suspension of the Shanghai County education subsidy, it is actually a separate issue. Before the division of governance rights between the province and the city, the Shanghai County Education Bureau took more than 38,000 yuan of municipal rental income, of which a portion was used as the administrative expenses of the Education Bureau, and the rest was used to handle the funding of Minhang Rural Middle School and Rural Normal School. The intention was to prepare a countermeasure after the transfer of governance rights, completely disregarding the facts of past years and the original fixed cases, and vaguely obtained approval from the former Central University. The means were particularly lacking in transparency. At the time of the handover, the expenditure statement submitted also listed 27,463 yuan of newly collected popular education mu tax and 1,122 yuan of municipal and rural subsidy committee salaries in the income item, in order to create the impression that the funds managed by this city were a superficial income exceeding expenditure, and the city was able to vaguely obtain an annual subsidy of 12,000 yuan in accordance with Article 5 of the Provincial and Municipal Division of Governance Rights Resolution. All educational institutions in Shanghai County that are located in the area that Shanghai Special Municipality should immediately take over should be transferred to the Special Municipality by the county, and the county's educational funds within the municipal and rural areas that should be transferred should be transferred to the Special Municipality. However, the County Education Bureau did not follow the regulations for uniform transfer, such as public school gardens, public science laboratories, Yu Garden Shangwen Road, Wu Garden Road, Zao Kui Street, Chuanxin Street, Yinggong Temple Road, Penglai Road, near the Pan Tang and other places, the annual income of which is 18,000 yuan, all belong to the educational assets in this area. Except for the current school garden and science laboratory, which have been transferred after several negotiations, all the equipment in the laboratory has been moved away. The Municipal Education Bureau estimated the value and approved it to be deducted from the County Education Fund. As for the remaining items, negotiations have been repeatedly carried out without any transfer. In order to implement the method of recovering and taking over, the Municipal Government has temporarily suspended the allocation of the County Education Fund, and has also sent a consultation to the Jiangsu Provincial Government to temporarily order corrections and supplementary payment. The Municipal Government's attitude is that if the County Education Bureau can respect the resolutions of the Provincial and Municipal Division of Governance Rights Conference and transfer the items that should be transferred first, then the education subsidy fee can also be allocated as usual. (East China News Agency)

56th

Commentary on the All-American Track and Field Championships 109

Besse Botte, 120-Yard High Hurdles; MacDonald, 35-Pound Weight Throw

丨Two World Records Broken丨

Lincoln, July 4th - The 56th All-American Track and Field Championships were held on the afternoon of July 4th in the city of Lincoln, Nebraska, amidst dim light and damp air. Track and field athletes from various states all fought bravely and appeared in full regalia. World records and national achievements emerged and were revealed one after another. The excellence of the results caused countless spectators to marvel. The competition was once stopped due to heavy rain, but the air turned dry in the evening. The entire field was illuminated by thousands of lights, shining as brightly as day, and the competition was able to continue and end perfectly. The Los Angeles Athletic Club won the championship with 41 points, and the New York Athletic Club came in second with 35 points. Here are excerpts of the most outstanding achievements for reference:

100 Yards - Frank Wykoff, a student of Gretel, is an invincible sprinter. He has crossed both the Atlantic and Pacific Oceans, and no one has ever been able to compete with him shoulder to shoulder. In the competition, he achieved 9.5 seconds in both the preliminary and final rounds, equaling the world record. In the final, he defeated Elmer Toppino of New Orleans. Toppino also achieved 9.5 seconds in the preliminary round and surpassed Eddie Tolan's previous record held in Michigan by five feet. Of the three timers, two recorded Wykoff's time as 9.5 seconds, while one recorded 9.3 seconds. If the time of the last person is valid, it would be a record never before seen by mankind.

220 Yards - Tolan of Michigan, unsuccessful in the 100 yards, vented his anger in the 220 yards, achieving a time of 21 seconds on the curved track, breaking the old record of 21.3 seconds. He and Metcalf ran side by side, but he put in the most effort and won by an inch. However, many observers believed that he seemed to have lost to a strong opponent.

Half Mile - Eddie Jenne, who set a record last year with 1 minute 53.4 seconds, broke his own record again this year, achieving a result of 1 minute 52.6 seconds.

One Mile - The New York Athletic Club swept the top three spots in this event. Lummis took first place with a time of 4 minutes 15 seconds. Lummis was in 12th place after the starting gun but took the lead at 500 yards and remained there until the end.

Two Miles - McGloughlin surpassed the crowd by 100 yards and won with a time of 10 minutes 11.6 seconds, breaking Mike Tivnan's 1919 record of 10 minutes 17.4 seconds.

Six Miles - Lewis Gergoly maintained his six-mile championship with a time of 31 minutes 26.4 seconds. He won against William Sansberg by jumping the last 15 yards.

120-Yard High Hurdles - Besse Botte, a handsome 19-year-old athlete from the New York Athletic Club, showed great skill on the waterlogged track, setting a world record with a time of 14.2 seconds, one of the most outstanding achievements of the competition. Tom Thompson's time of 14.4 seconds, set eleven years ago, is now a record of the past.

220-Yard Low Hurdles - The result of this event was also very outstanding. Bob Maxwell broke the previous record of 24 seconds held by Merley.

440-Yard Hurdles - Burke's achievement was also one of the highlights of the entire event, with a time of 54.12 seconds.

16-Pound Shot Put - The field was muddy, making throwing difficult. Only one person exceeded 50 feet, and that was Herman Brix, who has now won the championship for four consecutive years, with a result of 50 feet 8 and 1/4 inches.

35-Pound Weight Throw - The result of this event also broke a world record. The creator was New York police officer MacDonald, who weighs 350 pounds and is 52 years old. One of his throws reached a distance of 21 feet 6 inches, breaking the 18-year-old world record of 21 feet.

Hammer Throw - Lee Essak Dong, who weighs 230 pounds, threw the 56-pound hammer a distance of 35 feet 1 and 3/8 inches, taking first place. Second place went to MacDonald.

High Jump - Anton Burke once again maintained the national high jump championship, winning with a height of 6 feet 5 and 3/8 inches.

Relay Race - The relay race was divided into five events, including one mile, two miles, and four miles. The Los Angeles Athletic Club took first place with 18 points, and the New York Athletic Club came in second with 17 points.

Free Talk

World Snippets 110

— Haike

The King's Speaker

The London Conference, which shook the world on July 18th, was chaired by King George. The speaker he used was extraordinary, housed in a box made of gold and silver, engraved with the royal symbols and emblems, dazzling and imposing.

Vegetable Flavored Ice Cream

Most of the ice cream sold on the market is fruit-flavored, such as banana, lemon, orange, and mulberry, which are sweet and delicious and truly a gift for our summer. However, a large city in the United States has come up with a new trick, making several kinds of vegetable ice cream, such as radish, cabbage, and celery, which have a unique flavor and are very popular among men and women.

A Beautifully Decorated Chapel

Modern young men and women like to enjoy themselves in time, flocking to dance halls and nightclubs, and regard dull and monotonous chapels as a fearful road. In view of this, the pastor of St. John's Chapel in England spent 7,000 pounds to lay orange-yellow carpets in the chapel, install turquoise chairs, and paint the walls unusually magnificently. It is said that this can attract young men and women in general.

What I Know of the Eccentric Old Man of Jiangyin 111

— Zhang Gongyuan

Recently, the Free Talk section published an article by the owner of Qifeng Tower about an eccentric old man in Jiangyin who sleeps in a coffin at night. I think this was based on hearsay. What I know is very different from this. I am from Jiangyin, and I met the eccentric old man again last year. I will describe the whole story in order to correct the record.

The old man lives in Yuecheng Bridge in the southern countryside of Jiangyin, about half a mile away from the villa of Mr. Zhuang Xiang, a virtuous elder of my hometown. Last summer, I visited Mr. Zhuang for business. In the evening, I took a leisurely walk with him and happened to pass the old man's residence. We met the old man at the door, and he invited us in for a short sit-down. Looking up at his residence, I saw that it was a ancestral hall. In the central hall, there was a shrine about six or seven feet wide, with a spirit tablet in the middle. Under the shrine was a lacquered coffin, half buried in the ground, with the coffin lid placed beside it. The coffin was fully equipped with clothing and bedding, neatly arranged. I was secretly puzzled but did not ask. After sitting for a while, we bid farewell and left. On the way back, I asked Mr. Zhuang about it, and Mr. Zhuang told me the details one by one, so I learned about the old man's life and the beginning and end of placing the coffin. The old man was orphaned at a young age, knew a little about reading, and his family was poor. Since he came of age, he had been diligent, frugal, and hardworking, and devoted himself to farming. Before the age of forty, he had only been to the city twice. Gradually, he started a family. By the age of seventy, he had more than a hundred acres of good land. Between 1925 and 1926, the old man suddenly divided his land into three parts. One part was given to his son, and the other two parts were sold off to build a family ancestral hall with the money. The local gentry deeply praised him. The old man said with emotion: "Trees have roots, and water has sources. Can people alone not know how to think of their parents? I am unfortunate not to have been able to serve my parents. What I am doing now is the duty that a son should fulfill." The old man has a son, who is in his thirties and also able to manage the household. However, the old man often said that he was unworthy. When neighbors asked him, he said: "I relied on my own bare hands and worked hard for more than fifty years to have what I have today. Now my son cannot continue my ambition and work hard, but instead inherits my legacy and lives a comfortable life. How can he not be unworthy?" So he separated from his son and daughter-in-law, and lived alone in the ancestral hall with his five- or six-year-old grandson, not interfering in family affairs. The old man is naturally eccentric and has different views from others. On the day the ancestral hall was completed, he purchased a coffin, clothing, and other things for his afterlife, and buried half of the coffin under the shrine. When people asked him why, the old man said: "I am in my twilight years and may die at any moment, and my heart is already settled. What else do I have to be attached to? The only thing that is difficult is that I don't know when I will die. Now I have planned for it in advance, so I can die at any time and be placed in the coffin at any time, and I will not burden my descendants with my affairs after my death. This is beneficial to both me and my descendants. As for why the coffin is buried under the shrine, it is because I will be buried under this shrine in the future. I have told my children and grandchildren, and I believe that even if my children and grandchildren are unworthy, they will definitely follow my last wishes in the future. I was not able to serve my parents in life, which is a regret to the end of my days. In this way, I can be with my ancestors forever after death, and I can avoid leaving regrets. I don't want to be buried in the hills, associating with ghosts of different surnames, and my ancestors can have my companionship, so they will not be desolate and lonely. It is convenient for both of us. This is why I buried the coffin under the shrine." The old man is seventy-six or seventy-seven years old this year, but he looks like he is in his fifties. He eats like a strong man and walks briskly. If it is not too cold or hot, he can still travel more than thirty miles back and forth between the city and the countryside in half a day. He is also a national treasure. If someone can commend and promote him, I know that he will definitely be able to improve the customs and hone the vulgar habits. (Que Chou)

A Mock Birthday Celebration for Brother Zhang Shanzi at Fifty, and Requesting a Painting of a Tiger 112

— Da Ke

Mr. Zhang's tiger paintings are treasures of the world,

A single piece worth a hundred or a thousand strings of cash.

I say Mr. Zhang is not just painting tigers,

But simply writing his true self with each stroke.

Looking at your tiger's head and swallow's chin,

One knows without needing a fortune teller you are destined for greatness.

It's a pity you refuse to put down your brush,

And secure peace on the border, a thousand miles, as a marquis.

You came back, abandoning officialdom like worn-out shoes,

Building a home in Weitang to entertain your relatives.

Your whole family is fond of good things,

And dedicated to painting until old age.

Zi'ang painted horses, making them lie down,

Peeking into houses, he often incurred scolding.

Knowing you are by nature frank and open,

Dancing and jumping before guests, forgetting your cap and gown.

When the mood strikes, you look at your reflection and paint,

The spots on the canvas are your true spirit.

I laugh at Fubo for not understanding,

Chasing after horses and dogs in vain repetition.

This year you reach fifty, your first birthday,

In Dafen Hall, joyful guests gather.

My poem is not just to wish you well,

But also to ask for what you owe and speak frankly.

You once promised me a huge painting,

For a year I've waited, hesitant and disappointed.

Will "empty big" and "empty small" come true as omens?

The golden hairpins in my dream have no cause to exist. (Shanzi painted Twelve Golden Hairpins, all tigers)

When will the tiger guest push open my door?

Children will run away in fright, barking incessantly.

The poor fellow will gladly sweep the four walls,

From then on, becoming rich overnight, no longer poor.

I must also wish you a thousand, ten thousand years of life,

Like the hills, like the mountains, like the great cedar tree.

May you read this with a smile,

And ask the little scribe to record it for the gentry.

The Hong-Yang Rebellion and the Red-Goat Calamity 113

— Tian Hen

The two leaders of the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom happened to have one surnamed Hong (Xiuquan) and the other surnamed Yang (Xiuqing). Therefore, discussions of the Taiping events are referred to as the Hong-Yang Rebellion or the Red-Goat Calamity. Most people generally think that "Red-Goat" is a homophone for "Hong-Yang," that Hong-Yang came first and then the Red-Goat Calamity. But this is not the case. The term "Red-Goat" existed even before Hong-Yang. That is why it is said to be a coincidence. One day, a friend gave me an article about anecdotes from the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom era, with the small characters "Red-Goat Anecdotes" added to the title. He asked me to publish it in a certain newspaper. When I saw those small characters, I jokingly asked him what "Red-Goat" meant. He said seriously, "Red-Goat is Hong-Yang. What else is there to ask?" I said, "Why not write Hong-Yang then?" He said, "It's the same. You can write either one. But writing 'Red-Goat' feels more unique." I also said, "Who taught you that?" He said impatiently, "Who needs to teach me this? Hong-Yang, Red-Goat, aren't they the same? I've seen people write 'Red-Goat' countless times, just like writing '以' as '㠯' or '法' as '灋'. Why do you have to argue with me?" Seeing that he was becoming angry from impatience, I had no choice but to stop arguing and laugh it off. Now that I think about it, I'm afraid there are still young students who misunderstand Hong-Yang and Red-Goat as one and the same. It wouldn't hurt to explain it here. Originally, during the Chunyou reign of Emperor Lizong of the Zhao Song dynasty, there was a man named Chai Wang who compiled a book called the "Bing-Ding Tortoise Mirror." It covered the period from the 52nd year of King Zhuangxiang of Qin (Bingwu) to the 12th year of the Five Dynasties Han Tianfu (Dingwei), a total of 1,260 years. During that time, there were 21 years that were Bingwu or Dingwei. Coincidentally, in those years, there were disturbances in the country. Hence the name "Bing-Ding Tortoise Mirror." After compiling it, Chai Wang presented it to Emperor Lizong, hoping that Emperor Lizong would see it and use it as a lesson from the past to avoid misgovernment. Later generations referred to times of national disaster as "Red-Goat Calamity" because Bing belongs to fire, which is red, and Wei is the goat. The surnames of the leaders of the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom happened to be homophones of "Red-Goat." People at the time all considered the Qing Dynasty to be the legitimate rulers and the Taiping rebels to be bandits, so they also referred to it as the "Red-Goat Calamity." The draft written by Mr. So-and-so still had considerable respect for the Taiping and included the preface written by Sun Yat-sen for the history of the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom. If one understands the origin and meaning of the words "Red-Goat," one would not get angry and want to laugh out loud. Hehe.

Short News: Lin Feng'an, also known as the Master of Xihe, is famous in literary circles, especially for his calligraphy. Recently, seeing the severity of the floods in Baiyue, he made a charitable wish. He invited Zhang Yisheng, a famous painter from Yushan, to jointly organize a charity exhibition of calligraphy and paintings. Hundreds of works, large and small, were numbered in order, so that those who purchased coupons could enjoy the exhibition and draw lots on a whim to claim the corresponding items. Each coupon was valued at five yuan. After deducting expenses such as mounting and ink, the remaining proceeds were all allocated to the disaster area. It is said that the dates are August 15th and 16th, and the venue will be temporarily located at the Guangdong Primary and Secondary School on Baoyuan Road, Zhabei. (Ruo Xia)

Travels in India (74) 114

— Linghua

Before Islam entered India, the Greeks ruled India for 200 years. This small island is so strong, it's strange. We learn from India, but we haven't heard of India learning from anyone. They have a famous scholar named Aryabhata, who learned arithmetic from the Greeks. A friend mentioned a book called "India and Greece," but I didn't get to see it. Also, before Islam, there was a scholar named Bhaskara who already knew about the roundness of the earth. Xuanzang and Faxian are both honored guests in Indian history. They both wrote books about India.

The reasons for the rise and fall of Buddhism and Hinduism are worth studying. (1) Hinduism respects cows but sacrifices goats. Buddhism prohibits killing altogether. (2) Buddhism strives to send believers to spread the word abroad. Hinduism does not. (Now it is widely spread in the United States, but it has changed.) (3) Buddhism uses various languages to spread the word widely. In the past, Hinduism did not. The reason why Buddhism declined is that after many years, monks have high status, become arrogant and corrupt, and gradually lose the faith of the masses. When things flourish, they decline. Buddhism is also like this. 2. Foreigners have helped Hinduism. 3. Hinduism produced Shankaracharya during its revival, so Buddhism was overwhelmed by him and driven out of India, only preserving its last breath in Ceylon to the south and near the snowy mountains to the north.

As for the similarities and differences between the Nirgrantha and Buddhism, the creator of the Nirgrantha was also a prince who became a monk, hence the name "son" indicates his clan. His clan's name is Kshatriya, the prince is in the same position as the Buddha, the prince of the Pure Rice. 2. Their precepts and beliefs in Nirvana are the same. Their differences are that Buddhists believe in the Three Jewels. The three jewels believed in by the Nirgrantha are right belief, right knowledge, and right conduct. Also, the Nirgrantha believe that starvation is a good way to liberation. Buddha does not think so.

On the fifth day, I toured the Ganges with the students. The water is clear and the spring flow is very slow. There is a red iron bridge to the north. I looked at it but didn't cross it. The bank of the Ganges is also known as Lohanwei, the place where all the saints practice. There are those who support a large umbrella and sit and lie under it. There are those who sit on a bench. There are those who lie in a small room. There are the disabled sitting and begging, painting their faces with five colors, and their hair naturally formed into braids, probably because they don't comb it. There are also women among them, and there are many tourists. There are those who sell Taoist books, those who sell sweets, and those who tell stories. The students said that one of their relatives has now become an immortal. I approached him, but he did not speak to me. So I went to see him, and I saw a crowd surrounding a meditator. His whole body was only tied with a rope, and a two-inch cloth strip covered his genitals. He was sitting silently, and his body was not very thin. I guess he was eating. But he didn't close his eyes but took deep breaths. There was firewood in front of him, which is what the Buddhist scriptures call fire worship. He was sitting upright with his legs crossed. I stood for a long time and didn't see anything else. I went forward again. I often study zoology. The coiling of snakes, the hibernation of frogs, and the winter sleep of insects can all last for months without food, like dead people. Those who have deep skills in cultivation are also like this.

Rotary Club Stories

Women, Women (9) 115

— Yao Suifeng

It was already late, and he figured that Miss Ding must be eagerly waiting for him. But touching his pockets, he remembered that there was still one important thing he hadn't done. So he hurriedly jumped on the tram and went all the way to the main road.

Walking into a jewelry store, he embarrassedly took out the three pieces of gold jewelry from his pocket and said to the clerk, "These pieces are all out of style, please exchange them for cash!"

The clerk picked them up, looked at them carefully, put them on the scale to weigh them, and calculated carefully before saying, "A total of one tael and four mace. According to today's purchase price, it comes to one hundred and thirty-nine yuan, four jiao and five fen."

He was already very satisfied. After the cash and goods were cleared, he said again, "Please show me some diamond rings!"

The clerk changed his attitude and said very gently, "Please sit inside!"

When he got inside, the clerk pointed to a glass cabinet and told him to choose for himself. He looked at the cabinet, which was neatly arranged with many small boxes, each containing a diamond ring. Some were large, some were small, some had several stones set together, and some had a single stone. He felt that each one was pleasing, but he didn't know which one to choose. Then he thought that he didn't have much money, which made it even more difficult. Finally, he pointed to a relatively small one and asked the clerk to take it out.

"One hundred and ninety-five yuan!" The clerk looked at the number written under the box and read it out like that.

"That's too expensive!" he thought to himself. "Are there any cheaper ones?" he asked then.

"There are cheaper ones too, but I don't know how much money you are roughly prepared to spend?" the clerk said.

"A little over one hundred yuan would be good!"

Finally, he finally picked out one. He paid one hundred and twelve yuan and seven jiao, and finally got his wish for a diamond ring.

.

Walking out of the jewelry store, he felt much lighter and much more relaxed in his heart. He immediately hired a rickshaw to Tongfu Road, without even bargaining, just telling the rickshaw puller to run fast.

Meanwhile, Miss Ding had been waiting for a long time. Just as she was getting impatient, she suddenly heard the doorbell ring and told Qiuzi to open the door.

Qiuzi came back in and reported to Miss Ding with a surprised expression, "The one who came is a Mr. Li!"

"Did you refuse him?" Miss Ding was very unhappy.

"Yes! I know that Miss won't be meeting other guests today, so I have already refused him, saying that you are not at home." Qiuzi smiled slightly.

Securities: The Bond Market is Booming and Prices are Soaring 117

Consolidated Tax Bonds Soar by More Than Three Yuan, Other Bonds Also Rise by One or Two Yuan

Transaction Volume Reaches Over 25.5 Million

Yesterday, the bond market situation at the local securities exchange was that the spot market was as deserted as before, while the futures market suddenly became extremely lively. The enthusiasm of buyers and sellers was very strong. The September contracts had mostly opened. Major bonds all had huge transaction volumes, because bond prices had undergone huge changes and the market was lively. An investigation of the trend of bond prices showed that due to the optimistic situation in the north and a major turning point in the situation, the market was shrouded in buying interest as soon as the bonds opened. The demand and supply were very different, and prices soared sharply, continuing to rise significantly compared to the previous weekend. Later, selling interest also turned strong, but the buying side still dominated, and prices continued to rise. The trend has become much more peaceful. As a result, Consolidated Tax Bonds rose by three yuan, the 20 Customs Surtax Military Reduction Bonds and the 19 Customs Treaty Bonds rose by two yuan, and others also rose significantly. The volume of spot transactions was only 5,000 yuan, while futures transactions totaled over 25.5 million yuan. Arbitrage transactions were quite active. In addition, the transaction volume of Consolidated Tax Bonds has surpassed other bonds.

Cotton Yarn: Temporary Halt to the Market Decline 118

The cotton yarn market's declining trend has slightly subsided, but the overall trend remains weak. This is primarily due to the global cotton industry's weakness, exerting continuous pressure. Additionally, a certain merchant's uncovered positions continue to be dumped, further weakening market sentiment. Moreover, this year, various provinces within the country have suffered from flood disasters, resulting in significant damage to rice paddies. The harvest year is already considered poor, which will weaken farmers' purchasing power in the future, leading to a greater number of short sellers. However, the Rongxing firm's long positions remain calm and unmoved, making it difficult to be overly optimistic about the future.

Cotton Market Slightly Calmer 119

American Cotton Awaits Rebound

The cotton market is slightly calmer, but the overall situation remains very weak. This is because the global cotton industry is still in a pessimistic state. Moreover, there are reports of India devaluing and selling off its cotton, and the American cotton carryover has been announced at a massive 9.13 million bales. This huge amount of inventory is causing great unease. Therefore, merchants are taking a negative view of the overall trend and, as the tide turns, are painfully liquidating their long positions, leading to a loosening of the market. However, some are anticipating a potential rebound after several days of consecutive declines in American cotton prices. Considering the global situation, it is difficult to be optimistic about the future.

Indian Cotton Stable Last Week 122

Price Comparison with Liverpool Gradually Approaching

A dispatch from Mumbai on August 1st reported on the cotton market conditions during the past week, stating that local sentiment did not anticipate any decline in the cotton market. Therefore, despite the weakening of American cotton prices, there was no significant impact. The stability of the market was mainly due to exchange brokers buying when prices fell. As a result, the price comparison between Mumbai and Liverpool became closer. The spot cotton market is extremely quiet, with Japanese merchants showing no interest in buying. European demand remains stagnant. Local factories are maintaining their operational capacity, while Lancashire is focusing on new cotton and cheaper, medium-grade goods.
